<div id="review_574877984" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574877984" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574877984?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6590035-seize-the-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=fantastical-romance">fantastical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574877984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5505425902307538713">Bottom line: I liked it enough to finish it. I chuckled at some of Simi's antics. The sex is red hot. The language is clean. But the plot is tangled and obscure for most of the book — and that felt like a cheap trick — and the writing style is immature.<br/><br/>I've read several books in this long series. Will have to stop soon, cuz it's getting irritating. Cannot figure how this author gets such high marks. She needs to take a course in writing. Her books are filled with long info-dumps of past events, </span>
  <span id="freeText5505425902307538713" style="display:none">Bottom line: I liked it enough to finish it. I chuckled at some of Simi's antics. The sex is red hot. The language is clean. But the plot is tangled and obscure for most of the book — and that felt like a cheap trick — and the writing style is immature.<br /><br />I've read several books in this long series. Will have to stop soon, cuz it's getting irritating. Cannot figure how this author gets such high marks. She needs to take a course in writing. Her books are filled with long info-dumps of past events, poorly disguised as trances, dreams, mirrored images, mind-reading, etc. Too much passive telling, not showing. For example, I felt cheated when Tabitha told Amanda about a recent date — Valerius taking her to a fine restaurant. We heard the bare bones of a potentially vivid, compelling, and memorable scene. But no. Why couldn't we read that restaurant scene in real time, and see how it unfolds with that snooty waiter??<br /><br />Kenyon is also guilty of overkill. She does tragedy better than the Greeks. When they were still human, her heroes were all tortured, abused, reviled — forced to eat honest-to-god shit, and crucified, even! No subtlety. I like a sympathetic hero, but I don't want to feel and see the damn harp strings.<br /><br />Kenyon uses the same phrases over and over. In this book, our immortal, highly educated, and highly intelligent hero felt "stunned" more than 20 times. So stun me with a toothpick. Repeatedly, we hear how gorgeous he is — especially his ass. Also, Kenyons characters are described in the most superficial and basic terms: a blond, a brunette, etc. In one scene, a group of dark hunters were described merely by hair color. Really?<br /><br />This series is wildly popular, so I'm in the minority, but for me, this is silly, with too much <i>deux et machina.</i> All problems are far too easily resolved, making it impossible for me to become seriously captured by the plot. Life and death mean little in this book. It felt like playing cops and robbers when I was little -- hey presto! I'm alive again, in the game again!<br /><br />Romantic development: None. No slowly developing intimacy and trust here. Tabby falls for Val fast -- not sure why the sudden attraction -- and begins to seduce him in her kitchen within the first 24 hours. Val falls for Tabby when he first meets her, during a street fight against daemons.<br /><br />--- MAJOR PLOT SPOILERS ---<br /><br />These are the parts of the plot that bugged me. Don't click unless you want the story to be spoiled. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Too much <i>deux et machina.</i> Example: Everyone dies, murder and mayhem, etc. We're sad, bawling buckets. Oh, no, wait!! Have no fear, Ash is here to wave his magic around and make it all right. <br /><br />Another <i>deux et machina</i>: One character is immortal. Then mortal. Oops, we don't want him to die! Oh, heck, let's feed him ambrosia -- instant god!<br /><br />Valerius is a dark-hunter vampire, ~2000 years dead. Because of the vile atrocities his grandfather visited upon Kieryan (2000 years ago!) every paranormal in New Orleans hates him. Even those who have never met him. They gang up on him, bully him, mock him publicly, throw dirty water on his head, etc. Cruel. Petty. As in middle school. I could not admire these characters (Otto and Nick, especially). But their hatred made no logical sense, and thus seemed contrived, since it happened 2000 years ago and Valerius DIDN'T DO IT, as they ALL knew. Kenyon created this improbable conflict -- all this immature and unaccountable hostility -- just so Tabitha could be the first one to love poor pitiful Valerius, the first to fully accept him and stand up for him. Spare me.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But still, some parts were good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5505425902307538713" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1424531409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1424531409" />
    <a title="Gwen (The Gwendolyn Reading Method)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250598-gwen-the-gwendolyn-reading-method"><img alt="Gwen (The Gwendolyn Reading Method)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1395601703p2/2250598.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1424531409?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gwen (The Gwendolyn Reading Method)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gwen (The Gwendolyn Reading Method)" href="/user/show/2250598-gwen-the-gwendolyn-reading-method">Gwen (The Gwendolyn Reading Method)</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_14528346" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14528346" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/627337-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261273615p2/627337.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/14528346?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/627337-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/627337-tina?shelf=romance-paranormal">romance-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer14528346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13132771740803473477">Ok, here's the deal. I liked this book and I didn't like it. <br/><br/><b>Liked:</b><br/>Valerius. Again, Kenyon does superb when she speaks for/writes about the Dark Hunter. For some reason her writing comes alive for me when she centers on their past and their emotions.<br/><br/>The Ending: Once again, Kenyon begins with a whimper but ends with a bang. There were a few jaw dropping moments here that, from a reader perspective, were gratifying to see. I like it when a writer does something unpredictable and she did. Up to thi</span>
  <span id="freeText13132771740803473477" style="display:none">Ok, here's the deal. I liked this book and I didn't like it. <br /><br /><b>Liked:</b><br />Valerius. Again, Kenyon does superb when she speaks for/writes about the Dark Hunter. For some reason her writing comes alive for me when she centers on their past and their emotions.<br /><br />The Ending: Once again, Kenyon begins with a whimper but ends with a bang. There were a few jaw dropping moments here that, from a reader perspective, were gratifying to see. I like it when a writer does something unpredictable and she did. Up to this point the Dark-Hunter series hasn't really lived up to the 'Dark' part of its name. She really injected some darkness here and I think the story benefited from it.<br /><br /><b>kinda liked</b>:<br />Tabitha: On the plus side, Tabitha certainly did not fade into the background like some of the previous heroines have in the series. Her part wasn't overwhelmed by Valerius' part. However, I think that in an effort to make Tabitha so bold and brash and quirky, Kenyon made her off putting to me. She is a kick ass slayer who hangs out with utterly fabulous cross dressers and knows everyone. And even though she flitted through college and changed her major 12 times, she still managed, at a relatively young age, to earn a PhD in Ancient Civilizations. She can quickly and instantly psychoanalyze everyone perfectly. She speaks Latin, Greek and Italian flawlessly and was the lead singer in a metal band in College. <br /><br /><b>Disliked</b>:<br />The romance: Once again, I thought the romance was ho-hum. Just didn't engage me at all.<br /><br />Mean Girls: What is it with the whole Heathers mentality everyone had toward Valerius? In the previous books, Kenyon had created a plausible basis for Zarek, Kyrian and even to some extent Julian for their dislike/distrust of Valerius. But for it to extend to people who are friends of Nick's to not only dislike but to actively persecute him, lessens the impact she's going for with his story. Instead of creating some emotional resonance, it just makes me roll my eyes and wonder what else the "mean girls" have in store for him.<br /><br />Buzz Kills: I have only a hand full of pet peeves in books and Kenyon managed to hit about three of them in this one: 1) The Deus Ex Machina. I heartily dislike reading a book where all this stuff happens and then in a few pages in the end somebody comes by, waves a few fingers and *snap* all better. I think if things are FUBAR, then they need to either stay FUBAR or they need to be fixed in a logical, organic way. She's been using Acheron as a swoop in and clean up guy and it is, imo, a cheat. 2) "Arms Akimbo". Honestly, nobody but the late Kathleen Woodiwiss should use that phrase. and 3) "Spitfire" again, a phrase describing a (usually red-head) woman which should have been retired in romance novels circa 1989.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13132771740803473477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gEJO9rvexLezPziTqq6iZ3VG6BIVUJ6DN2pnMYrBvl8S56nyNxr6bS/gq5JsTxZrrTZkGb0ZBmMQqWedh4y57g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ixa8Qd0Q0ST/AEnoJdMXSbM1CTr68NrqXHVAk7eOc3mxs1tFUdTv/mPf2unjMqNFa0WFMVK5Qgp7tkA/usN0yA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

With legions of fans known as Paladins (thousands of whom proudly sport tattoos from her series and who travel from all over the world to attend her appearances), her books are always snatched up as soon as they appear on store shelves. Since 2004, she had placed more than 80 novels on the New York Times list in all formats including manga and graphic novels. Her current series are: Dark-Hunters, Chronicles of Nick and The League, and her books are available in over 100 countries where eager fans impatiently wait for the next release.
